Bunce, was digitized in 2007 by the UW Digital Collections Center.<sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">[109]</a></sup> The Kohler Art Library is open to the public.</p>\n<p>The online catalog for UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison Libraries is MadCat.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">[110]</a></sup> It includes bibliographic records for books, periodicals, audiovisual materials, maps, music scores, microforms, and computer databases owned by over 40 campus libraries, as well as records for items that are on order. The UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison Libraries website provides access to resources licensed for use by those affiliated with UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison, in addition to those openly available on the <a href="/wiki/World_Wide_Web" title="World Wide Web">World Wide Web</a>.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Museums">Museums</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Museums">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:State-historical-society.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/State-historical-society.jpg/220px-State-historical-society.jpg" width="220" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/State-historical-society.jpg/330px-State-historical-society.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/84/State-historical-society.jpg/440px-State-historical-society.jpg 2x" data-file-width="600" data-file-height="406" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:State-historical-society.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWisconsin Historical Society</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/UW%E2%80%93Madison_Geology_Museum" title="UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison Geology Museum">Geology Museum</a> features rocks, minerals, and fossils from around the world. Highlights include a blacklight room, a walk-through cave, and a fragment of the <a href="/wiki/Meteor_Crater" title="Meteor Crater">Barringer meteorite</a>. Some noteworthy fossils include the first dinosaur skeleton assembled in Wisconsin (an <i><a href="/wiki/Edmontosaurus" title="Edmontosaurus">Edmontosaurus</a></i>), a <a href="/wiki/Shark" title="Shark">shark</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Squalicorax" title="Squalicorax">Squalicorax</a></i>) and a floating colony of <a href="/wiki/Crinoids" class="mw-redirect" title="Crinoids">sea lilies</a> (<i><a href="/wiki/Uintacrinus" title="Uintacrinus">Uintacrinus</a></i>), both from the <a href="/wiki/Cretaceous" title="Cretaceous">Cretaceous</a> chalk of <a href="/wiki/Kansas" title="Kansas">Kansas</a>, and the Boaz <a href="/wiki/Mastodon" title="Mastodon">Mastodon</a>, a found on a farm in southwestern Wisconsin in 1897.<sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">[111]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Chazen_Museum_of_Art" title="Chazen Museum of Art">Chazen Museum of Art</a>, formerly the Elvehjem Museum of Art, maintains a collection of paintings, drawings, sculpture, prints and photographs spanning over 700 years of art.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">[112]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The university\'s Zoological Museum maintains a collection of approximately 500,000 zoological specimens, which can be used for research and instruction. A special collection contains skeletons, artifacts, and research papers associated with the <a href="/wiki/Gal%C3%A1pagos_Islands" title="Gal\xc3\xa1pagos Islands">Gal\xc3\xa1pagos Islands</a>. Since 1978, the UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison Zoological Museum has been one of only three museums granted permission by the Ecuadoran Government to collect anatomical specimens from the Gal\xc3\xa1pagos Islands.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">[113]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/L._R._Ingersoll_Physics_Museum" title="L. R. Ingersoll Physics Museum">L. R. Ingersoll Physics Museum</a> contains a range of exhibits demonstrating <a href="/wiki/Classical_physics" title="Classical physics">classical</a> and <a href="/wiki/Modern_physics" title="Modern physics">modern physics</a>. Many of the exhibits allow for hands-on interaction by visitors. The museum also has a number of historical instruments and pictures on display.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">[114]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Effigy_mounds">Effigy mounds</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Effigy mounds">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/220px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" width="220" height="146" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/330px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG/440px-Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG 2x" data-file-width="4928" data-file-height="3264" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Willow_Drive_Mounds-DA119.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nWillow Drive Effigy Mounds</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison claims more distinct archaeological sites than on any other university campus.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">[115]</a></sup> The campus contains four clusters of <a href="/wiki/Effigy_mounds" class="mw-redirect" title="Effigy mounds">effigy mounds</a> located at Observatory Hill, Willow Drive, Picnic Point, and Eagle Heights. These sites, reflecting thousands of years of human habitation in the area, have survived to a greater or lesser degree on campus, depending on location and past building activities. Surviving sites are marked and fenced on the campus, ensuring that they are not disturbed. Wisconsin statutes protect effigy mounds by giving them a five-foot buffer zone.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">[116]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-117" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-117">[117]</a></sup> The <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison_Lakeshore_Nature_Preserve" title="University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison Lakeshore Nature Preserve">Lakeshore Nature Preserve Committee</a> is endeavoring to "\xe2\x80\xa6safeguard beloved cultural landscapes," through aggressive enforcement of measures for the preservation of such zones and advocating for broader buffers where possible.<sup id="cite_ref-118" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-118">[118]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Athletics">Athletics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Athletics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Wisconsin Badgers</a></div>\n<p>The University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison sports teams participate in the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a>\'s <a href="/wiki/Division_I-A" class="mw-redirect" title="Division I-A">Division I-A</a>. With the exception of lightweight <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_Crew" title="Wisconsin Badgers Crew">Wisconsin Badgers Crew</a>, the university\'s athletic programs compete in the <a href="/wiki/Big_Ten_Conference" title="Big Ten Conference">Big Ten Conference</a>. The women\'s <a href="/wiki/Ice_hockey" title="Ice hockey">hockey</a> program competes in the <a href="/wiki/Western_Collegiate_Hockey_Association" title="Western Collegiate Hockey Association">Western Collegiate Hockey Association</a> (WCHA), while the <sup id="cite_ref-119" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-119">[119]</a></sup> men\'s and women\'s crew programs compete in the <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association_of_Rowing_Colleges" title="Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges">Eastern Association of Rowing Colleges</a> and <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Association_of_Women%27s_Rowing_Colleges" title="Eastern Association of Women\'s Rowing Colleges">Eastern Association of Women\'s Rowing Colleges</a>, respectively. The school\'s <a href="/wiki/Fight_song" title="Fight song">fight song</a> is <i><a href="/wiki/On,_Wisconsin!" title="On, Wisconsin!">On, Wisconsin!</a></i>. The school\'s mascot is Buckingham U. Badger, commonly referred to as "<a href="/wiki/Bucky_Badger" title="Bucky Badger">Bucky Badger</a>". The athletic director is <a href="/wiki/Barry_Alvarez" title="Barry Alvarez">Barry Alvarez</a>.</p>\n<p>2005\xe2\x80\x932006 marked the first time in school history that four Badger teams won national championships in the same academic year.<sup id="cite_ref-120" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-120">[120]</a></sup> In the fall, the men\'s cross country team won its fourth national championship. The winter season was highlighted by the men\'s and women\'s ice hockey teams both winning national titles. The year was capped off in the spring with the women\'s lightweight crew taking its third straight <a href="/wiki/Intercollegiate_Rowing_Association" title="Intercollegiate Rowing Association">Intercollegiate Rowing Association</a> national crown. In 2008, both men\'s and women\'s crew teams claimed national titles.<sup id="cite_ref-121" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-121">[121]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Football">Football</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Football">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_football" title="Wisconsin Badgers football">Wisconsin Badgers football</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/220px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/330px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a7/Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg/440px-Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Camp_Randall_Stadium_2.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\n<a href="/wiki/Camp_Randall_Stadium" title="Camp Randall Stadium">Camp Randall Stadium</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The Badgers play <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> at <a href="/wiki/Camp_Randall_Stadium" title="Camp Randall Stadium">Camp Randall Stadium</a>. The head coach is Paul Chryst. Before the fourth quarter of every game at Camp Randall, the crowd jumps around to <a href="/wiki/House_of_Pain" title="House of Pain">House of Pain</a>\'s song "<a href="/wiki/Jump_Around" title="Jump Around">Jump Around</a>". After every game, the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_Marching_Band" title="University of Wisconsin Marching Band">University of Wisconsin Marching Band</a> plays popular songs during the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Wisconsin_Marching_Band#Traditions" title="University of Wisconsin Marching Band">Fifth Quarter</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-122" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-122">[122]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-123" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-123">[123]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-124" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-124">[124]</a></sup> The Badgers won three <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> Championships under Alvarez in 1994, 1999, and 2000. In 2006, Bielema led the Badgers to a school record 11-win regular season and to 12 overall wins, defeating <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arkansas" title="University of Arkansas">Arkansas</a> in the <a href="/wiki/Capital_One_Bowl" class="mw-redirect" title="Capital One Bowl">Capital One Bowl</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-125" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-125">[125]</a></sup> The Badgers lost to <a href="/wiki/Texas_Christian_University" title="Texas Christian University">TCU</a> in the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Rose_Bowl_Game" title="Rose Bowl Game">Rose Bowl</a> Championship on January 1, 2011. In the 2011 season, the Badgers defended the B1G championship title to go to the 2012 Rose Bowl Championship. The Badgers lost to Oregon 45\xe2\x80\x9338 in the highest-scoring Rose Bowl of all time.<sup id="cite_ref-126" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-126">[126]</a></sup> The Badgers made it to the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rose_Bowl" title="2013 Rose Bowl">2013 Rose Bowl</a> for their third consecutive Rose Bowl appearance. Brett Bielema took the Arkansas football head coaching position before the game and Barry Alvarez took over as a one-game interim coach.<sup id="cite_ref-Barry_Alvarez_will_coach_Wisconsin_in_the_Rose_Bowl_127-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Barry_Alvarez_will_coach_Wisconsin_in_the_Rose_Bowl-127">[127]</a></sup> The Badgers lost to Stanford 14-20 for Barry Alvarez\'s first Rose Bowl loss, he had previously won it three times.<sup id="cite_ref-128" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-128">[128]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="Men\'s_basketball"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Men.27s_basketball">Men\'s basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: Men\'s basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/220px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/330px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Kohl_Center_inside.jpg/440px-Kohl_Center_inside.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_inside.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMen\'s basketball game as seen from the student section at the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_basketball" title="Wisconsin Badgers men\'s basketball">Wisconsin Badgers men\'s basketball</a></div>\n<p>The Badgers have made 18 consecutive appearances (1999\xe2\x80\x932016) in the <a href="/wiki/NCAA_Men%27s_Division_I_Basketball_Championship" class="mw-redirect" title="NCAA Men\'s Division I Basketball Championship">NCAA Tournament</a>, with <a href="/wiki/Final_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Final Four">Final Four</a> visits in 2000, 2014 and 2015, an <a href="/wiki/Elite_Eight" title="Elite Eight">Elite Eight</a> appearance in 2005, and Sweet Sixteen appearances in 2003, 2008, 2011, 2012, and 2016.<sup id="cite_ref-129" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-129">[129]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bo_Ryan" title="Bo Ryan">Bo Ryan</a> was the head coach from 2001 to 2015. Greg Gard was named interim coach. The <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Badgers</a> play at the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a>, where the student fans are known as the <a href="/wiki/Grateful_Red" title="Grateful Red">Grateful Red</a>. In the 2006\xe2\x80\x932007 season, the Badgers attained their highest AP ranking in school history (#1 Feb. 19\xe2\x80\x9325), garnering 35 first-place votes.<sup id="cite_ref-130" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-130">[130]</a></sup> The Badgers earned their only NCAA National Championship in 1941.</p>\n<h3><span id="Women\'s_basketball"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Women.27s_basketball">Women\'s basketball</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: Women\'s basketball">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_women%27s_basketball" title="Wisconsin Badgers women\'s basketball">Wisconsin Badgers women\'s basketball</a></div>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ice_hockey">Ice hockey</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: Ice hockey">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers_men%27s_ice_hockey" title="Wisconsin Badgers men\'s ice hockey">Wisconsin Badgers men\'s ice hockey</a></div>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/220px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/330px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a8/Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg/440px-Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1152" data-file-height="768" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Kohl_Center_hockey.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nMen\'s <a href="/wiki/Hockey" title="Hockey">hockey</a> game played at the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a></div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>Badger ice hockey first became a men\'s varsity sport in 1922. Although dropped after the 1934\xe2\x80\x9335 season, it again became a varsity sport in the 1963\xe2\x80\x9364 season. The men\'s team played in the <a href="/wiki/Dane_County_Coliseum" class="mw-redirect" title="Dane County Coliseum">Dane County Coliseum</a> until moving to the <a href="/wiki/Kohl_Center" title="Kohl Center">Kohl Center</a> (capacity 15,359) in the fall of 1998. The first ice hockey game played at the Kohl was the Hall of Fame game against the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Notre_Dame" title="University of Notre Dame">University of Notre Dame</a>. From 1999 to 2012 the men\'s team led the nation in college hockey attendance, setting an NCAA attendance record (averaging 15,048) during the 2009\xe2\x80\x9310 season, which surpassed their previous record set in 2006\xe2\x80\x9307.<sup id="cite_ref-131" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-131">[131]</a></sup></p>\n<p><a href="/wiki/Bob_Johnson_(ice_hockey_b._1931)" class="mw-redirect" title="Bob Johnson (ice hockey b. 1931)">Bob Johnson</a>, nicknamed "Badger Bob" by fans, took over the reins in 1966. Johnson coached the Badger men to three national championships in 1973, 1977 and 1981. Jeff Sauer coached the Badger men to two more titles in 1983 and 1990. <a href="/wiki/Mike_Eaves" title="Mike Eaves">Mike Eaves</a>, member of the 1977 NCAA title team, coached the Badger men\'s team to its sixth national championship in 2006. The six Badger titles rank 4th in NCAA men\'s ice hockey history.<sup id="cite_ref-132" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-132">[132]</a></sup> Eaves\' 2010 squad advanced to the national championship game during the Badgers\' 11th appearance in the men\'s <a href="/wiki/Frozen_Four" class="mw-redirect" title="Frozen Four">Frozen Four</a> before bowing to <a href="/wiki/Boston_College" title="Boston College">Boston College</a>.</p>\n<p>The school\'s strong ice hockey tradition gained another dimension with the addition of a women\'s team that began play in the 1999\xe2\x80\x932000 season. Coached by <a href="/wiki/Mark_Johnson_(hockey_player)" class="mw-redirect" title="Mark Johnson (hockey player)">Mark Johnson</a>, son of "Badger Bob" and another member of the men\'s 1977 title team, the Badger women won their first NCAA championship on March 26, 2006. The dual 2006 titles marked the first time that both the men\'s and women\'s Division I NCAA hockey titles were won by the same school in the same year.<sup id="cite_ref-133" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-133">[133]</a></sup> The women\'s team repeated as national champions in 2007 with a victory over the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota-Duluth" class="mw-redirect" title="University of Minnesota-Duluth">University of Minnesota-Duluth</a> and in 2009 with a victory over <a href="/wiki/Mercyhurst" class="mw-redirect" title="Mercyhurst">Mercyhurst</a>. The team set the NCAA women\'s hockey attendance record on February 15, 2014, in a game against Minnesota.<sup id="cite_ref-134" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-134">[134]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Rivalries">Rivalries</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: Rivalries">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright">\n<div class="thumbinner" style="width:227px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg/225px-Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg" width="225" height="149" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg/338px-Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1f/Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg/450px-Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg 2x" data-file-width="3216" data-file-height="2136" /></a>\n<div class="thumbcaption">\n<div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Badgers_carrying_Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>\nBadgers celebrate their win by carrying Paul Bunyan\'s Axe around Camp Randall after the 2009 game.</div>\n</div>\n</div>\n<p>The <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Badgers" title="Wisconsin Badgers">Wisconsin Badgers</a>\' most notable rivalry within the Big Ten is with the <a href="/wiki/Minnesota_Golden_Gophers" title="Minnesota Golden Gophers">University of Minnesota</a>, which is the <a href="/wiki/List_of_NCAA_college_football_rivalry_games" title="List of NCAA college football rivalry games">most-played rivalry</a> in Division 1-A football.<sup id="cite_ref-135" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-135">[135]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-136" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-136">[136]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-137" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-137">[137]</a></sup> In their annual <a href="/wiki/College_football" title="College football">college football</a> game, the teams compete for <a href="/wiki/Paul_Bunyan%27s_Axe" class="mw-redirect" title="Paul Bunyan\'s Axe">Paul Bunyan\'s Axe</a>. The two universities also compete in the <i>Border Battle</i>, a year-long athletic competition in which each team\'s wins earn points for their university.</p>\n<p>Men\'s basketball rivalries include <a href="/wiki/Michigan_State_Spartans_men%27s_basketball" title="Michigan State Spartans men\'s basketball">Michigan State</a>, <a href="/wiki/Illinois_Fighting_Illini_men%27s_basketball" title="Illinois Fighting Illini men\'s basketball">Illinois</a> and non-conference, in-state <a href="/wiki/Marquette_Golden_Eagles_men%27s_basketball" title="Marquette Golden Eagles men\'s basketball">Marquette</a>.</p>\n<p>The Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison men\'s and women\'s hockey teams\' most recognized rivals are the <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gophers" class="mw-redirect" title="Golden Gophers">Golden Gophers</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota" title="University of Minnesota">University of Minnesota</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Fighting_Sioux" class="mw-redirect" title="Fighting Sioux">Fighting Sioux</a> of the <a href="/wiki/University_of_North_Dakota" title="University of North Dakota">University of North Dakota</a>. Other rivals include the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Denver" title="University of Denver">University of Denver</a>, <a href="/wiki/Colorado_College" title="Colorado College">Colorado College</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michigan_Tech_University" class="mw-redirect" title="Michigan Tech University">Michigan Tech</a>, <a href="/wiki/University_of_Minnesota_Duluth" title="University of Minnesota Duluth">University of Minnesota Duluth</a>, and <a href="/wiki/St._Cloud_State_University" title="St. Cloud State University">St. Cloud State</a>.</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Mascot">Mascot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: Mascot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Bucky_Badger" title="Bucky Badger">Bucky Badger</a></div>\n<p>The school mascot is an <a href="/wiki/Anthropomorphism" title="Anthropomorphism">anthropomorphized</a> <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badger</a> named <a href="/wiki/Bucky_Badger" title="Bucky Badger">Bucky</a> who dons a sweater affixed with the UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison athletic logo (currently the red "Motion W"). Beginning in 1890, the university\'s first Bucky Badger was a live, temperamental and unruly <a href="/wiki/Badger" title="Badger">badger</a> who was quickly retired. Although the nickname of the Wisconsin teams remained the "Badgers", it was not until Art Evans drew the early caricature version of Bucky in 1940 that today\'s recognizable image of Bucky was adopted. In 1949, a contest was held to name the mascot, but no consensus was reached after only a few entries were received. In reaction, the contest committee chose the name Buckingham U. Badger, or "Bucky", for short.</p>\n<p>At Wisconsin football games in the 1920s live mascots were used to inspire fans. The animals used included a black bear, a bonnet monkey, and live badgers. 1949 was the first year a student sporting a papier-m\xc3\xa2ch\xc3\xa9 badger head appeared; this subsequently replaced the use of live badgers.<sup id="cite_ref-138" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-138">[138]</a></sup></p>\n<p>The team\'s nickname originates from the <a href="/wiki/List_of_U.S._state_nicknames" title="List of U.S. state nicknames">state nickname</a>. In the 1820s, many lead miners and their families lived in the mines in which they worked until adequate above-ground shelters were built, and thus were compared to badgers.<sup id="cite_ref-139" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-139">[139]</a></sup></p>\n<p>In 2009, Fulton Market Films produced the documentary <i>Being Bucky</i> which followed the lives of seven Wisconsin students who take on the role of Bucky Badger.<sup id="cite_ref-140" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-140">[140]</a></sup> <i>Being Bucky</i> won "Best Documentary Film" at the <a href="/wiki/Wisconsin_Film_Festival" title="Wisconsin Film Festival">Wisconsin Film Festival</a> and went on to play in local Wisconsin movie theaters.<sup id="cite_ref-141" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-141">[141]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_life">Student life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: Student life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<p>Over 750 student organizations or clubs register with the Center for Leadership and Involvement (CFLI) at UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison each year.<sup id="cite_ref-142" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-142">[142]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Media">Media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=35" title="Edit section: Media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Student_publications">Student publications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=36" title="Edit section: Student publications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison is the only university in the country with two daily student newspapers:<sup id="cite_ref-143" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-143">[143]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-144" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-144">[144]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-145" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-145">[145]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-146" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-146">[146]</a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Cardinal" title="The Daily Cardinal">The Daily Cardinal</a></i>, founded in 1892 and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Badger_Herald" title="The Badger Herald">The Badger Herald</a></i>, founded in 1969. <i><a href="/wiki/The_Onion" title="The Onion">The Onion</a></i> was founded in 1988 by two UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison juniors, and was published in Madison before moving to New York City in 2001. It is also the home of <i><a href="/w/index.php?title=The_Madison_Misnomer&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="The Madison Misnomer (page does not exist)">The Madison Misnomer</a></i>, an undergraduate comedy newspaper, founded in 2007.</p>\n<p>UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison is also home to one of only two nationally distributed undergraduate international studies journals in the country. The Journal of Undergraduate International Studies (JUIS) is a competitive publication that features peer-reviewed academic articles. It was founded in 2003 by David Coddon with the support of the University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison Leadership Trust.</p>\n<h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Campus_radio">Campus radio</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=37" title="Edit section: Campus radio">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4>\n<p>The University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison campus radio station is <a href="/wiki/WSUM" title="WSUM">WSUM</a> 91.7 FM, "The Snake on the Lake".<sup id="cite_ref-147" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-147">[147]</a></sup> Historically, UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison has been home to a collection of student run radio stations, a number of which stopped broadcasting after run-ins with the United States <a href="/wiki/Federal_Communications_Commission" title="Federal Communications Commission">Federal Communications Commission</a> (FCC). The current radio station, WSUM, began in 1997 in a <a href="/wiki/Webcast" title="Webcast">webcast</a> only format because of the prolonged battle to get an FCC license and construct a tower. This lasted five years until February 22, 2002, when the station started broadcasting over <a href="/wiki/Frequency_modulation" title="Frequency modulation">FM</a> airwaves at 91.7 from its tower in <a href="/wiki/Montrose,_Wisconsin" title="Montrose, Wisconsin">Montrose, Wisconsin</a>. The radio station currently has around 200 volunteer DJs and eight paid managers. All UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison students, as well as a limited number of community members, are eligible to participate in running the station. WSUM remains entirely free format, which means that the on-air personnel can showcase a large variety of music and talk programming at their discretion with few limitations. WSUM has garnered many awards from the Wisconsin Broadcasters Association for their news, play-by-play broadcasts of Badger athletic events, and unique <a href="/wiki/Public_service_announcements" class="mw-redirect" title="Public service announcements">public service announcements</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-148" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-148">[148]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Organizations">Organizations</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=38" title="Edit section: Organizations">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>Among the student organizations at the school include chapters of the fraternities <a href="/wiki/Acacia_(fraternity)" title="Acacia (fraternity)">Acacia</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-149" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-149">[149]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Chi_Omega" title="Alpha Chi Omega">Alpha Chi Omega</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-150" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-150">[150]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Delta_Phi" title="Alpha Delta Phi">Alpha Delta Phi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-151" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-151">[151]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Gamma_Rho" title="Alpha Gamma Rho">Alpha Gamma Rho</a><sup id="cite_ref-152" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-152">[152]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Delta_Chi" title="Delta Chi">Delta Chi</a><sup id="cite_ref-153" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-153">[153]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Sigma_Alpha" title="Sigma Alpha">Sigma Alpha</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-154" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-154">[154]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Chi_Sigma" title="Alpha Chi Sigma">Alpha Chi Sigma</a> was founded at the university in 1902.</p>\n<p>Religious student organizations include affiliates of the <a href="/wiki/Christian" title="Christian">Christian</a> organizations <a href="/wiki/Cru_(Christian_organization)" title="Cru (Christian organization)">Cru</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-155" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-155">[155]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Athletes_in_Action" title="Athletes in Action">Athletes in Action</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-156" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-156">[156]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Chi_Alpha_Campus_Ministries" title="Chi Alpha Campus Ministries">Chi Alpha Campus Ministries</a><sup id="cite_ref-157" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/Christian_Legal_Society" title="Christian Legal Society">Christian Legal Society</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-158" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-158">[158]</a></sup></p>\n<p>UW is also home to student vehicles teams such as <a href="/wiki/UW_Hybrid_Vehicle_Team" title="UW Hybrid Vehicle Team">UW Hybrid Vehicle Team</a>, <a href="/wiki/Badgerloop" class="mw-redirect" title="Badgerloop">Badgerloop</a>, and Formula SAE teams.<sup id="cite_ref-159" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-159">[159]</a></sup></p>\n<h3><span id="MTV\'s_College_Life"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="MTV.27s_College_Life">MTV\'s <i>College Life</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=39" title="Edit section: MTV\'s College Life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<p>On April 13, 2009, MTV premiered the <a href="/wiki/Reality_series" class="mw-redirect" title="Reality series">reality series</a> <i><a href="/wiki/College_Life" title="College Life">College Life</a></i> about the day-to-day lives of eight UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison freshmen.<sup id="cite_ref-160" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> The show was created by UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison alumnus <a href="/wiki/David_Wexler_(writer/director)" class="mw-redirect" title="David Wexler (writer/director)">David Wexler</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-161" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup> According to MTV,<sup id="cite_ref-162" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> the students did the filming for the series, but not the editing. During production, the university pulled its support of the show. Subsequently, a disclaimer was aired at the beginning of each episode stating that UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison does not endorse the program. Eight episodes had aired as of February 22, 2010.</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Notable_alumni_and_people">Notable alumni and people</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=40" title="Edit section: Notable alumni and people">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison_people" title="List of University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison people">List of University of Wisconsin\xe2\x80\x93Madison people</a></div>\n<p>As of 2017, UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison had more than 427,000 living alumni. Although a large number of alumni live in Wisconsin, a significant number live in Illinois, Minnesota, New York, California, and Washington, D.C.<sup id="cite_ref-alumni_163-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alumni-163">[163]</a></sup></p>\n<p>UW\xe2\x80\x93Madison alumni, faculty, or former faculty have been awarded 21<sup id="cite_ref-164" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> Nobel Prizes and 34 Pulitzer Prizes.<sup id="cite_ref-alumni_163-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-alumni-163">[163]</a></sup></p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=41" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul>\n<li><a href="/wiki/University_Square_(Madison)" title="University Square (Madison)">University Square (Madison)</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/UW_Hybrid_Vehicle_Team" title="UW Hybrid Vehicle Team">UW Hybrid Vehicle Team</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Weinert_Center" title="Weinert Center">Weinert Center</a> for Entrepreneurship</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/World_Cocoa_Foundation" title="World Cocoa Foundation">World Cocoa Foundation</a> (Partnership)</li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Badgerloop" class="mw-redirect" title="Badgerloop">Badgerloop</a> - a SpaceX Hyperloop Competition Team</li>\n</ul>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=University_of_Wisconsin%E2%80%93Madison&amp;action=edit&amp;section=42" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div class="reflist columns references-column-width" style="-moz-column-width: 30em; -webkit-column-width: 30em; column-width: 30em; list-style-type: decimal;">\n<ol class="references">\n<li id="cite_note-1"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-1">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><cite class="citation web"><a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.uwalumni.com/home/travel/askabe_campus.aspx">"Ask Abe Archives \xe2\x80\x93 Campus Traditions"</a>.
